      "content after edit": [
        "Then, the obtained vector is converted into a probability vector whose elements sum to one through the softmax layer. The vector input to the softmax layer is also called the logit vector. In this case, the larger the logit value, the higher the probability value after softmax, so at the first time step, it will predict the category 'o' corresponding to the last dimension, which currently has a total probability of 84%. However, our ground truth class is the character that appears after 'h'â€”that is, the second category. Ultimately, we train the model to maximize the assigned probability for this ground truth class.\n\nMore specifically, training proceeds by minimizing the cross-entropy loss, which is the negative logarithm of the probability assigned to the ground truth.\n\nSimilarly, at the second time step, the sequence information up to 'he' is well accumulated in the h2 vector here, then transformed into a vector of hidden dimensionality through the output layer W_{hy}, and passed through softmax. From the resulting probability vector, the ground truth class at this point is the character 'l' that follows 'he'. We take the log of the assigned probability 0.5 in the third dimension, add a negative sign, and minimize this cross-entropy loss during training."
      ]

      "content after edit": [
        "Then, the obtained vector is converted into a probability vector whose elements sum to one through the softmax layer. The vector input to the softmax layer is also called the logit vector. In this case, the larger the logit value, the higher the probability value after softmax, so at the first time step, it will predict the category 'o' corresponding to the last dimension, which currently has a total probability of 84%. However, our ground truth class is the character that appears after 'h'â€”that is, the second category. Ultimately, we train the model to maximize the assigned probability for this ground truth class.\n\nMore specifically, training proceeds by minimizing the cross-entropy loss, which is the negative logarithm of the probability assigned to the ground truth.\n\nSimilarly, at the second time step, the sequence information up to 'he' is well accumulated in the h2 vector here, then transformed into a vector of hidden dimensionality through the output layer W_{hy}, and passed through softmax. From the resulting probability vector, the ground truth class at this point is the character 'l' that follows 'he'. We take the log of the assigned probability 0.5 in the third dimension, add a negative sign, and minimize this cross-entropy loss during training."
